The Czech man still had a second Pilgrim, which Matsumara killed with [Garruk Relentless](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk+Relentless), which quickly became [Garruk, the Veil-Cursed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk%2C+the+Veil-Cursed). Juza landed [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader), a card that was seeing a lot of play on the weekend, while Matsumara contented himself with getting himself a Wolf from Garruk before matching Juza, [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) for [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader).


That parity didn't last long, with Juza's [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) taking out the Crusader, which allowed his own double strike man to end Garruk's presence on the board. Back came Matsumara with [Hero of Bladehold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Bladehold) and Avacyn Pilgrim. Juza was fighting hard, but this was much more of an uphill battle than in game one. On the plus side, he still had four cards in hand, to just one for his Japanese opponent.


After a long pause for thought, Juza opted for [Mortarpod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mortarpod), which was dwarfed by [Mikaeus, the Lunarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mikaeus%2C+the+Lunarch) for three. Juza's own Legend once again denied his opponent an edge in what was turning into a real game of power punches expertly avoided. [Garruk Relentless](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk+Relentless) was next for Matsumara. You just know what Juza did - yes, another [Garruk Relentless](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk+Relentless)! Then he added his own Planeswalker to the board in [Elspeth Tirel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth+Tirel). There aren't many more powerful effects in the game than an in-the-house Planeswalker, but an in-the-house [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan) might just be one of them.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gphir11/LSV2.jpg)
*LSV Token*

Juza added three Soldiers to his team. [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader), [Mortarpod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mortarpod) with a token, three Soldiers, Elspeth at two Loyalty. On the other side, [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan), a 2/2 Wolf, Avacyn Pilgrim, [Hero of Bladehold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Bladehold), and [Mortarpod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mortarpod), also equipping a token. Juza decided - with some justification - that he needed more men on board, and Elspeth hit the graveyard in exchange for three more 1/1s for the Czech player. Every bit as important as his creatures, though, were his lands, and while Matsumara had [Kessig Wolf Run](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kessig+Wolf+Run) in play, Juza had [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township), and mana to use it.


Matsumara didn't like that state of affairs, and when [Primeval Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primeval+Titan) attacked he was able to rectify the situation, searching out two copies of [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) for himself. Although [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) blocked and killed the Titan, it was still at the expense of five live as the [Kessig Wolf Run](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kessig+Wolf+Run) allowed the Titan to trample over Juza's double strike blocker. Juza activated his [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township), and it was back to the Czech man to call the shots.


In came everything, and I mean everything. It was like World War III on the battlefield, with tokens and creatures and dice flying everywhere. [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) fortified Juza's men once more, and the net result was 16 damage coming through to Matsumara, whose board now comprised no more than an Avacyn Pilgrim and a lonely [Mortarpod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mortarpod). The dust cleared, and Juza advanced to 8-0.


Martin Juza 2 - 0 Toshikazu Matsumara



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gphir11/The%20End%20Game.jpg)
*The End Game*



Snap Keep
---------


*by Nate Price* 

There was no card in *Innistrad* that received the same amount of hype, or even anywhere near the same amount even, as [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). The long-prophesized appearance of Tiago Chan's Invitational card came bearing the impressive burden of having to live up to not only the staggering hype, but the power level of the abilities it bore. As a two-drop, it has flash and allows players to replay an instant or sorcery from their graveyard. If there is anything that **Magic** history has taught me, it's that giving blue players access to instants with that kind of versatility leads down a dangerous road ([Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command)?).




![Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Snapcaster+Mage)


Whatever. This isn't about whether or not [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Snapcaster%2BMage) lives up to its hype or not. I could care less about that. I mean, the card has been printed. It is going to do what it is going to do. And that's what I'm going to focus on: what it does.


There are 236 instants and sorceries in the [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage)'s Standard toolbox. Most of those are never going to see play, but it is at least a significant number to have as a starting point. Over the past few weeks, as Standard has become more defined, so have the spells of choice.


Finding a deck featuring [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) without finding [Forbidden Alchemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forbidden+Alchemy) is more likely attributed to someone forgetting to write a card down on their decklist than an innovative build. With the ability to sift through the deck, as well as feed the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster with some juicy targets, the cards seem like they were designed to work together. To complement the sift and card drawing, many blue-based decks are also running some combination of [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), [Think Twice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Think+Twice), and even [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination) in some rare cases. The average winning Solar Flare deck from the last few Standard events has about three [Forbidden Alchemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forbidden+Alchemy), three [Think Twice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Think+Twice), and eschews the other two cards entirely.




![Forbidden Alchemy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forbidden+Alchemy)


Ok, so the card drawing isn't that varied. The countermagic is a little better, but more because of the sideboard options than anything. With [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate), [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak), [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate), and [Flashfreeze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flashfreeze) available, there are a few more situational cards that start to work their way into decks. The average deck runs four [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak)s and two to three [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate)s. [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate) shows up, but not in enough numbers to warrant a spot in the maindeck. It does however warrant a spot as a one-of in the sideboard, right alongside [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate) and [Flashfreeze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flashfreeze).




![Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mana+Leak)


Looking at the removal starts to get interesting. The types of [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster bait played depends on the version of the deck you're playing. The main differentiation comes between UB Control decks, the UW Control decks, and Solar Flare, which dips into both white and black. The decks featuring black have access to [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) (which kills everything, I've been told), [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat), [Wring Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wring+Flesh), [Tribute to Hunger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribute+to+Hunger), [Geth's Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geth%27s+Verdict), and [Black Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Sun%27s+Zenith), and [Victim of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Victim+of+Night). For the white inclined, you get [Celestial Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Purge), [Revoke Existence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revoke+Existence), and [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment). All of them can play [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember). Since I've been looking at Solar Flare so far, I'll continue. The average Solar Flare deck seems to be running three [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade)s, one or two [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment)s, and one more single-target removal spell, most frequently [Tribute to Hunger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribute+to+Hunger). In the sideboard, there is usually one or two more single-target spells, usually [Celestial Purge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Purge) and [Revoke Existence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revoke+Existence). While the compiled list has shorn down the long list of possibilities to these select few, there is a wide variety amongst the decks of the last slot or two. The variation increases as you start to look at UB Control decks, which run a higher amount of removal than their Solar Flare counterparts.




![Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Doom+Blade)


After that, the last cards in the toolbox are utility spells. These include [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements), [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites), [Surgical Extraction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surgical+Extraction), and [Memoricide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memoricide). In Solar Flare, there tend to be two [Unburial Rites](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unburial+Rites) and three [Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timely+Reinforcements). The other cards don't seem to have a home in the maindeck, but there are two sideboard slots devoted to some combination of Extraction and [Memoricide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memoricide), more often than not Extraction.




![Timely Reinforcements](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Timely+Reinforcements)


While these examples deal primarily with the UB-based versions of [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Snapcaster%2BMage), there have been instances of other colors getting in on the fun. There have been reports of RUG decks coming in with a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Snapcaster%2BMage) or two, returning such hits as [Slagstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slagstorm), [Arc Trail](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arc+Trail), and [Beast Within](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Beast+Within), which I've heard are pretty good against the green-based decks in the format. These decks are much rarer than their UBW counterparts, but they do provide an interesting avenue to take things.




Round 9 Roundup
---------------


*by Rich Hagon* 

At the start of the final round of the day, six players still had 100% records at 8-0. Only three could end the day with that perfect record still intact.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gphir11/Daniel%20Pham%20v%20Martin%20Juza.jpg)
*Daniel Pham 0 - 2 Martic Juza*

The Czech Level 8 really came good today, with a triumphant return to form, having missed day two on his last four GP appearances. 'It's so good to run good again' he said with a relieved grin.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gphir11/The%20End%20Game.jpg)
*Takuma Morofuji 1 - 2 Riu Satou*

Former National Champion Morofuji had a great day, but couldn't complete the marathon, losing out to Satou.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gphir11/Sui%20Xin%20v%20Masahiro%20Sunaga.jpg)
*Sui Xin 2 - 0 Masahiro Sunaga*

Finally, it was the man from Beijing, Sui Xin, who claimed the third 100% record overnight.


Congratulations to our three leaders - six more rounds separate them from the final top 8 of the Japanese Grand Prix season.
